// Learn more about Tauri commands at https://tauri.app/develop/calling-rust/
#[tauri::command]
fn greet(name: &str) -> String {
    format!("Hello, {}! You've been greeted from Rust!", name)
}

#[cfg_attr(mobile, tauri::mobile_entry_point)]
pub fn run() {
    tauri::Builder::default()
        .plugin(tauri_plugin_opener::init())
        .invoke_handler(tauri::generate_handler![greet])
        .run(tauri::generate_context!())
        .expect("error while running tauri application");
}


# File: C:\Users\Slyphur\Documents\interceptor\src-tauri\src\main.rs

#![cfg_attr(not(debug_assertions), windows_subsystem = "windows")]

use std::fs::OpenOptions;
use std::io::Write;
use tauri::command;
use windows::core::*;
use windows::Win32::Graphics::Printing::{EnumPortsW, PORT_INFO_2W};
use windows::Win32::Foundation::{BOOL, ERROR_INSUFFICIENT_BUFFER, WIN32_ERROR};
use bytemuck;
use windows::Win32::System::Registry::*;
use std::path::Path;


/// Helper: Convert a 0-terminated wide string pointer to a Rust String
fn wide_ptr_to_string(ptr: PWSTR) -> String {
    unsafe {
        if ptr.0.is_null() {
            return String::new();
        }
        let slice = std::slice::from_raw_parts(ptr.0, wcslen(ptr.0));
        String::from_utf16_lossy(slice)
    }
}

/// Find length of a wide string (null-terminated)
unsafe fn wcslen(ptr: *const u16) -> usize {
    let mut len = 0;
    while *ptr.add(len) != 0 {
        len += 1;
    }
    len
}

/// Enumerate all current printer ports
#[command]
fn get_ports() -> std::result::Result<Vec<String>, String> {
    println!("Starting port enumeration...");
    let mut needed_bytes = 0u32;
    let mut returned = 0u32;
    let level = 2u32;

    unsafe {
        // First call to determine buffer size
        println!("Making first EnumPortsW call to get buffer size...");
        let ok: BOOL = EnumPortsW(None, level, None, &mut needed_bytes, &mut returned);
        if ok.as_bool() {
            return Err("Unexpected success on first EnumPortsW call".to_string());
        }

        let err_code = windows::Win32::Foundation::GetLastError();
        println!("First call result - needed_bytes: {}, error code: {:?}", needed_bytes, err_code);
        
        let windows_error = err_code.unwrap_err();
        let error_code = windows_error.code().0;
        
        // Convert HRESULT to Win32 error code by masking out the facility and severity
        let win32_error = error_code & 0xFFFF;
        println!("Win32 error code: {:#x}", win32_error);
        
        // ERROR_INSUFFICIENT_BUFFER is 122 (0x7A)
        if win32_error != 0x7A {
            return Err(format!(
                "EnumPortsW first call failed unexpectedly. Windows error: {:?} ({})",
                windows_error,
                get_windows_error_message(win32_error as u32)
            ));
        }

        if needed_bytes == 0 {
            return Err("EnumPortsW indicated 0 bytes required.".to_string());
        }

        // Allocate buffer and get ports
        println!("Allocating {} bytes for port information...", needed_bytes);
        let mut buffer = vec![0u8; needed_bytes as usize];
        let ok2: BOOL = EnumPortsW(
            None,
            level,
            Some(&mut buffer),
            &mut needed_bytes,
            &mut returned
        );
        
        println!("Second call result - returned ports: {}", returned);
        
        if !ok2.as_bool() {
            let err_code = windows::Win32::Foundation::GetLastError().unwrap_err();
            return Err(format!(
                "EnumPortsW second call failed. Windows error: {:?} ({})",
                err_code,
                get_windows_error_message(err_code.code().0 as u32)
            ));
        }

        // Parse out the port names
        let port_info_array = buffer.as_ptr() as *const PORT_INFO_2W;
        let count = returned as usize;
        let mut port_names = Vec::with_capacity(count);
        for i in 0..count {
            let pi2 = &*port_info_array.add(i);
            let port_name = wide_ptr_to_string(pi2.pPortName);
            println!("Found port: {}", port_name);
            port_names.push(port_name);
        }

        if port_names.is_empty() {
            return Err("No printer ports were found.".to_string());
        }

        println!("Successfully enumerated {} ports", port_names.len());
        Ok(port_names)
    }
}

/// Helper function to get Windows error messages
use windows::Win32::System::Diagnostics::Debug::{FormatMessageW, FORMAT_MESSAGE_FROM_SYSTEM};
use windows::core::PWSTR;
use std::ptr;

fn get_windows_error_message(error_code: u32) -> String {
    let mut buffer: [u16; 512] = [0; 512];

    unsafe {
        let len = FormatMessageW(
            FORMAT_MESSAGE_FROM_SYSTEM,
            None,  // `None` replaces `ptr::null()`
            error_code,
            0,
            PWSTR(buffer.as_mut_ptr()),  // Convert raw pointer to PWSTR
            buffer.len() as u32,
            None,  // `None` replaces `ptr::null_mut()`
        );

        if len > 0 {
            return String::from_utf16_lossy(&buffer[..len as usize]).trim().to_string();
        }
    }

    format!("Unknown error ({})", error_code)
}


/// Convert Rust string to UTF-16 wide chars
fn to_wide_chars(s: &str) -> Vec<u16> {
    use std::os::windows::ffi::OsStrExt;
    std::ffi::OsString::from(s)
        .encode_wide()
        .chain(std::iter::once(0))
        .collect()
}

/// Verify that the PrinterInterceptor is properly installed
fn verify_printer_interceptor() -> std::result::Result<(), String> {
    // Check if the DLL exists
    let dll_path = Path::new(r"C:\Windows\System32\PrinterInterceptor.dll");
    if !dll_path.exists() {
        return Err("PrinterInterceptor.dll not found in System32. Please run install.ps1 as administrator.".to_string());
    }

    // Check registry key
    unsafe {
        let mut hkey = HKEY::default();
        let result = RegOpenKeyExW(
            HKEY_LOCAL_MACHINE,
            w!("SYSTEM\\CurrentControlSet\\Control\\Print\\Monitors\\PrinterInterceptor"),
            0,
            KEY_READ,
            &mut hkey
        );
        
        if let Err(error) = result {
            return Err(format!(
                "PrinterInterceptor registry key not found (error: {:?}). Please run install.ps1 as administrator.",
                error
            ));
        }
        
        RegCloseKey(hkey);
    }

    Ok(())
}

/// Command: Set Active Output Port (only 1 argument)
#[command]
fn set_active_port(real_port: String) -> std::result::Result<(), String> {
    // First verify the installation
    verify_printer_interceptor()?;

    let pipe_name = r"\\.\pipe\PrinterInterceptorPortPipe";
    let max_retries = 3;
    let mut last_error = None;

    // Try a few times with a delay between attempts
    for attempt in 0..max_retries {
        if attempt > 0 {
            println!("Retrying to open pipe (attempt {}/{})", attempt + 1, max_retries);
            std::thread::sleep(std::time::Duration::from_secs(1));
        }

        match OpenOptions::new().write(true).open(pipe_name) {
            Ok(mut file) => {
                let wide = to_wide_chars(&real_port);
                match file.write_all(bytemuck::cast_slice(&wide)) {
                    Ok(_) => return Ok(()),
                    Err(e) => last_error = Some(format!("Error writing to pipe: {e}")),
                }
            }
            Err(e) => {
                last_error = Some(format!(
                    "Could not open pipe (attempt {}/{}): {e}. Make sure PrinterInterceptor.dll is installed and running. Try running 'rundll32.exe C:\\Windows\\System32\\PrinterInterceptor.dll,StartInterceptorThreads' as administrator.",
                    attempt + 1,
                    max_retries
                ));
            }
        }
    }

    Err(last_error.unwrap_or_else(|| "Unknown error occurred".to_string()))
}

/// Command: Inject Print Command via Named Pipe
#[command]
fn inject_print_command(text: String) -> std::result::Result<(), String> {
    let mut data = text.into_bytes();
    data.push(b'\n'); // Add newline for ESC/POS printers

    let pipe_name = r"\\.\pipe\PrinterInterceptorPipe";
    match OpenOptions::new().write(true).open(pipe_name) {
        Ok(mut file) => {
            if let Err(e) = file.write_all(&data) {
                return Err(format!("Error writing print data to pipe: {e}"));
            }
            Ok(())
        }
        Err(e) => Err(format!("Could not open pipe: {e}")),
    }
}

fn main() {
    tauri::Builder::default()
        .invoke_handler(tauri::generate_handler![
            get_ports,
            set_active_port,
            inject_print_command,
        ])
        .run(tauri::generate_context!())
        .expect("Error running Tauri application");
}

// Tauri doesn't have a Node.js server to do proper SSR
// so we will use adapter-static to prerender the app (SSG)
// See: https://v2.tauri.app/start/frontend/sveltekit/ for more info
import adapter from "@sveltejs/adapter-static";
import { vitePreprocess } from "@sveltejs/vite-plugin-svelte";

/** @type {import('@sveltejs/kit').Config} */
const config = {
  preprocess: vitePreprocess(),
  kit: {
    adapter: adapter(),
  },
};

export default config;

import { defineConfig } from "vite";
import { sveltekit } from "@sveltejs/kit/vite";

// @ts-expect-error process is a nodejs global
const host = process.env.TAURI_DEV_HOST;

// https://vitejs.dev/config/
export default defineConfig(async () => ({
  plugins: [sveltekit()],

  // Vite options tailored for Tauri development and only applied in `tauri dev` or `tauri build`
  //
  // 1. prevent vite from obscuring rust errors
  clearScreen: false,
  // 2. tauri expects a fixed port, fail if that port is not available
  server: {
    port: 1420,
    strictPort: true,
    host: host || false,
    hmr: host
      ? {
          protocol: "ws",
          host,
          port: 1421,
        }
      : undefined,
    watch: {
      // 3. tell vite to ignore watching `src-tauri`
      ignored: ["**/src-tauri/**"],
    },
  },
}));
